Causality and Created Things
intermediate
5 min
Al-Shahrastani's Two-Aspect Theory of Human Action
Al-Shahrastani distinguishes between divine creation and human acquisition using the specific description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Shahrastani's two-aspect theory of human action: how an act is entirely God's creation in its existence but is attributed to the human in its specific moral quality, which is the basis of moral responsibility.

Core Idea
An act's existence is from God; its moral quality is from the human.

Al-Shahrastani, a prominent Ash'ari theologian, refines the doctrine of acquisition (kasb) by distinguishing two aspects of every human act. On one hand, the act's existence as a created entity is solely from God; on the other, its specific quality—whether it is obedience or disobedience—is attributed to the human. This distinction preserves God's exclusive creative power while explaining human moral accountability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation side by side. Notice that the passage discusses two perspectives: movement as existence vs. movement as a particular moral act (e.g., prayer, theft).
Pay attention to the words 'من حيث' which signal the two different aspects.
2
Identify the two attributions
Find where the passage attributes the act to God (creation, knowledge, no inherence) and where it attributes it to the human (specific description, locus, attribution as 'he is praying').
God creates the movement; the human performs the specific act.
3
Understand the role of specific description
The passage states that the command and prohibition address the specific description (e.g., 'pray, do not steal'). That specific quality is what makes an act obedience or disobedience and what merits reward or punishment.
The existence of the act is neutral; only its moral quality matters for evaluation.
4
Reflect on the solution to a theological problem
Consider how this two-aspect theory solves the tension between God as the sole creator and human responsibility. Humans do not create the act's existence, but they are responsible for its moral quality through acquisition (kasb).
This aligns with Ash'ari theology that avoids attributing any share in creation to humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختار الشَّهْرَسْتانيُّ مذهبَ القاضي ، وفرَّقَ بين وجهي الاختراع والكسب : بأنَّ الحركة مِنْ حيثُ هي حركةٌ تُنسَبُ إلى فعلِ اللهِ تعالى إيجاداً واختراعاً ، ويلزمُ مِنْ ذلكَ علَمُهُ بهَا مِنْ جميع وجوهها وأَنَّهُ لا يفعلُ في ذاتِهِ ولا يتَصفُ بها اتصاف قيام ، فلا تُضافُ إِليهِ مِنَ العبدِ مِنْ حيثُ خصوصها ، فيُقالُ : أوجدها وأحدثها ، ولا يُقالُ : إِنَّهُ متحرك بها ، وتُنسَبُ إلى العبدِ مِنْ حيثُ خصوصها ؛ وهو كون تلك الصفةِ صلاةً أو غصباً أو سرقةً ، ولا تأثير لقدرةِ العبدِ إلا في ذلكَ الوجه ، ولا يُشترَطُ علمُهُ بالفعل مِنْ كلّ وجه ، وذاتُهُ محل فعلِهِ وكسبه ، وتكونُ صفةٌ لهُ ، فيُقالُ : إِنَّهُ مُتحرِّكُ وساكن ومُصلِّ وغاصب ، وإن اتصلَ بهِ أمرُ فوقع على موافقته.. سُمِّيَ طاعةً وعبادةً ، وإن اتصلَ بهِ نهي فوقع على خلافه.. سُمِّيَ معصيةٌ وجريمة ، وذلك الوجه هو المكلَّف به ، وهو الذي توجَّهَ الخطاب بهِ ، فقيل : صل ، ولا تسرق ، ولا تغصب ، وهو المقابل بالثواب والعقاب ، والمدح والذم ، لا مِنْ حيثُ إِنَّهُ موجود
And al-Shahrastani chose the doctrine of al-Qadi, and distinguished between the two aspects of creation (ikhtirāʿ) and acquisition (kasb): that movement, insofar as it is movement, is attributed to the act of God the Exalted as bringing into existence and creation; and from that follows His knowledge of it from all its aspects, and that He does not act in His essence nor is He described by it with a description of inherence, so it is not attributed to Him from the servant from the aspect of its particularity. Thus it is said: He brought it into existence and originated it, and it is not said: He is moving by it. And it is attributed to the servant from the aspect of its particularity, which is that the attribute be prayer, or usurpation, or theft. And there is no effect of the servant's power except in that aspect, and his knowledge of the act from all aspects is not required, and his essence is the locus of his act and acquisition, and it becomes an attribute for him, so it is said: he is moving and still and praying and usurping. And if a command attaches to it and it occurs in conformity to it, it is called obedience and worship; and if a prohibition attaches to it and it occurs contrary to it, it is called disobedience and crime. And that aspect is what one is obligated concerning, and it is what the address is directed to, so it is said: pray, do not steal, do not usurp. And it is what is met with reward and punishment, praise and blame, not insofar as it is existent.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of al-Shahrastani's position on the distinction between divine creation (ikhtirāʿ) and human acquisition (kasb) within the Ash'ari framework. He adopts al-Qadi's view that human power acts on the most specific description. The distinction is made on the basis of two perspectives on the same act (e.g., movement). From the perspective of its existence as a created entity, the act is entirely from God: He brings it into existence, knows it in all its aspects, and does not become qualified by it in the sense of inherence. For example, we say 'God created the movement,' but we do not say 'God is moving by it.' From the perspective of its specific description (khṣūṣiyya)—that it is prayer, theft, etc.—the act is attributed to the human servant. The servant's power only affects that specific aspect, not the existence. Consequently, the servant is described as 'praying' or 'stealing' because his essence is the locus (maḥall) of the act as acquired. This specific description is the subject of religious obligation (taklīf): it determines whether the act is obedience or disobedience, and it is what merits reward or punishment. The existent act qua existence is not the object of moral evaluation—only its specific quality is. This preserves God's exclusive role as creator while allowing human moral responsibility.

Key Terms
اختراع
كسب
أخص وصف
خصوص
طاعة
معصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Acquisition (kasb) means the human creates the act's existence or a part of it.
Correction: In al-Shahrastani's view, the human's power only affects the act's specific moral quality (e.g., being prayer or theft), not its existence. The existence remains entirely God's creation.

Checkpoint
According to al-Shahrastani, which aspect of an act is the subject of reward and punishment?
A) The act's existence as a created entity.
B) The act's specific description, such as being prayer or theft.
C) The act's universal essence.
D) The act's relation to God's will.

Key Takeaway
Al-Shahrastani resolves the tension between divine omnipotence and human responsibility by attributing the existence of acts to God and their specific moral qualities to human acquisition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform an act of worship like prayer, do you sense that its very existence is a gift from God while you are only responsible for its 'prayer-ness'? How would your awareness of God's presence change if you consciously separated the two aspects in your mind?
?
If your act's existence is entirely from God, then your sin is not an independent rebellion but a misdirection of God-given existence. Does that humble you about your disobedience or make you more accountable? What does it mean that God creates the motion of your hand as it steals or hits?
?
Al-Shahrastani says the servant's essence is the locus of the act. When you sin, do you feel that your very self becomes the site of that sin, and that God's knowledge encompasses it? How does that thought compel you to purify your intentions before your next action?
